<Words> What has Christianity deeply connected with throughout its historical process? It is the mountain. Therefore, today I would like to speak to you under the title "The Sad Heart of Jesus Going to the Mountain."

As you already know well from the scripture, please recall the image of Jesus ascending the Mount of Transfiguration during this hour. 

Jesus, who ascended to that mountain, was the representative of the entire providence of history, the representative of that entire era, and furthermore, the representative of all future descendants. However, please recall that he did not ascend the Mount of Transfiguration with a joyful heart, but with a solemn, sad, and lonely heart.

We must recognize that this event was not merely a solemn event that ended at that moment, but a significant decision that would have repercussions from the time before Jesus, during Jesus' time, and even after Jesus. 

Whenever Jesus faced a significant task, we know that he sought out high mountains. After fasting for 40 days in the wilderness, Jesus faced the three great temptations from Satan, carrying within himself concerns for heaven, humanity, and all creation, needing to clearly distinguish between the two. For Jesus, who bore such responsibilities, that scene was a solemn and significant moment where he had to discern between heaven and Satan, between the works of heaven and the works of Satan. Even then, Jesus was led by Satan to the top of a mountain and was tested.

Looking at the mountains associated with Jesus, there was the mountain he was led to by Satan in the wilderness, the Mount of Transfiguration where he went to decide the issue of bearing the final cross due to the disbelief of the Jewish people, and then there was the Garden of Gethsemane where he prayed decisively to cross over the path of death to Golgotha. We must recall these facts.

We must think about how Jesus' footsteps moved as he sought out these mountains, what kind of sorrow and grief he felt, and how he manifested himself. We must deeply reflect on the image of Jesus going into the wilderness 2,000 years ago. Otherwise, we will not be able to understand the desperate heart of Jesus as he fought against Satan.

In the three great temptations during his journey in the wilderness, the place where Jesus overcame Satan and achieved the final victory was also at the top of a high mountain. The steps he took in the wilderness, rejected by the chosen John the Baptist and betrayed by the Jewish people, were steps taken with a sorrowful heart that no one on this earth has been able to experience until today.

Jesus was the only begotten son of heaven, the one who would resolve 4,000 years of history, and he appeared as a victory standard that heaven could boast about before that era and for all generations to come. We must recall the sorrowful heart of Jesus as he went into the wilderness alone, leaving behind the people, abandoning the denomination, and even leaving behind the chosen John the Baptist and the family of Joseph, without any friends.

With a sense of mission to establish such a historical condition of indemnity, Jesus, while fasting for 40 days, reflected on what? He felt more than anyone else the responsibility that he must indemnify and restore the sorrowful path that his ancestors had walked. We must realize this fact at this time.

Then, what thoughts must Jesus have had as he was led by Satan to the top of the high mountain during the process of the three temptations? He was filled with a solemn heart, worrying about the entire course of 4,000 years of history, whether he could set up the shield of final victory to overcome Satan.

As Jesus walked in the wilderness, he must have recalled that after Adam and Eve were expelled from the Garden of Eden, their descendants would also have to wander in search of that garden due to their loss of it. When he thought of the historical ancestors who had lived in the sorrowful garden after being expelled from God, Jesus could not help but think seriously about the noun "mountain" in relation to the mountain.

Jesus must have recalled Noah, who appeared 1,600 years later, who endured all hardships for 120 years at the foot of Mount Ararat to restore the original state of Adam and Eve, who were expelled from the Garden of Eden. He must have thought that Noah lived such a life for the sake of today’s self. Jesus must have envisioned Noah longing for his own image standing on the mountain.

Recalling the loyalty of the ancestors who sought the mountains, Jesus must have thought of Abraham, who, after making a mistake with the sacrifice, received the command to offer Isaac as a burnt offering and was heading toward the mountain. He could not help but recall the solemn heart of Abraham as he took his late-born son Isaac to Mount Moriah.

For whom was Isaac to be offered as a sacrifice? For whom did Abraham have to offer his only son, Isaac? Of course, it was for his father, and at the same time, it was for the coming Messiah. He must have recalled this historical fact.

Next, he must have thought of Moses. He went through 40 years in the palace and 40 years in the Midian wilderness. He must have thought about the scene where God appeared to Moses in the burning bush at the foot of Mount Horeb, making a new promise.

He could not help but recall the scene where Moses met God at Horeb and established an unchanging bond, as well as the providence of God to inevitably remove Satan from this universe and the loyalty of Moses towards that will, which created a bond between God and Moses.

Moses, who received the command to lead the chosen people of Israel from Egypt to the land of Canaan, was an 80-year-old man who had suffered in the wilderness. However, his gaze and demeanor were those that pierced the heart of heaven. We could not help but recall Moses, who had such a standard of heart.

Furthermore, from the standpoint of having led 600,000 people into the wilderness, which had no food or clothing, Moses, who bore the responsibility of leading them to the land of Canaan, must have climbed Mount Sinai out of concern that they might go astray. At the top of Sinai, Moses fasted and prayed for 40 days and nights. Afterward, he received the word of God and came down, and Jesus could not help but recall Moses' situation.

Moses went up to Mount Sinai to fast for 40 days solely for the sake of heaven and to prepare the way for the Messiah, and furthermore, to establish the restored nation that God sought. He could not help but think of this.

Next, he must have recalled Elijah, who confronted the priests of Baal on Mount Carmel. For whom was all of this? As Jesus walked while recalling this, he thought that the fact that the ancestors prayed before heaven to find a solution at the top of the mountain was all for God and, furthermore, for himself. Jesus bore a solemn heart as he recalled this historical connection to the mountain. Today, we too must reflect on this inner world of Jesus.

The footsteps of Jesus being led by Satan in the wilderness were not steps taken for his own sake. As you know through the principle, Jesus had to fulfill personal restoration, environmental restoration, and world restoration, and he carried this in his heart as he went through this symbolic process to the mountaintop. He prepared himself for the great test that would unfold at that place, intending to establish a tradition as a historical new ancestor and inherit the heart of heaven, and we must understand that Jesus ascended to the mountaintop following Satan.

Jesus had a solemn heart regarding his purpose more than anyone else. We must recognize that he went out into the wilderness with a burning heart to grasp and subdue Satan, standing firm with a determination stronger than any historical ancestor. We must also recognize that Jesus stood alone at the mountaintop.

When Jesus recalled this historical course, he felt that he must have a solemn resolve for himself, and at the same time, when he thought of the chosen people of Israel, he felt an indescribable sorrow due to the historical responsibility.

God established John the Baptist on this earth to pave a new way to fulfill heaven's will. He sent John the Baptist in advance to prepare the ground to welcome the Messiah, but John the Baptist disbelieved Jesus. As a result, the people and the chosen ones, whom God had blessed as the chosen people for 4,000 years, disappeared, and Jesus had to find the lost multitude again. We must understand this situation of Jesus.

Standing in such a position, Jesus could not help but feel despair. When he thought of all the chosen people and established groups of that era, he was overwhelmed with sorrow. However, as Jesus examined the motives and origins that created such a situation and considered the historical feelings up to that time, he realized that the being responsible for this was Satan. Here, Jesus faced the temptation of Satan with a firm resolution to surely overcome him. You must not forget this solemn scene.

Jesus could not help but seek the mountain again due to his lonely situation. Satan showed him all the kingdoms of the world and their glory, saying, "If you will fall down and worship me, I will give you all these things." (Matt 4:8-9) However, Jesus resolutely rejected Satan. Thus, he established a standard of victory before Satan. Moreover, he obtained a standard that could connect to the historical and epochal sorrow, and he had to descend again toward the chosen Israel and the established Judaism, which served as a stepping stone for historical connection.

Thus, Jesus went to the people of Israel and Judaism with the standard of victory established during his journey in the wilderness, but they did not welcome him at all. Rather than welcoming him, they persecuted, opposed, and mocked him wherever he went and stayed. The initial rejection when he went out into the wilderness was already disappointing and infuriating, but when he looked at the Judaism and the people of Israel raising their opposition against him, who had returned with the condition of victory over Satan, he was truly filled with indescribable grief and sorrow. We must think of Jesus in such a position today.

Even in the midst of a persecuted and chaotic environment, he prayed for them from the mountaintop to turn the nation and denomination back, and he fought against Satan throughout his three years of public life, but he saw no results. Therefore, in the end, he ascended the Mount of Transfiguration with the heart that he must awaken the ignorant people even if it meant his own death.

Jesus, knowing that no effort as a human could yield results, set out with a heartfelt desire to save those who were connected to the historical and epochal relationships, those who were related to the heart of heaven, even if it meant becoming a sacrifice and shedding his blood and flesh. However, the place he sought was not a magnificent palace. It was not the house of a disciple who could accept him, nor the house of the people of that nation, nor the houses of the Jews at that time. The place he went was the Mount of Transfiguration. You must reflect on the sorrowful heart of Jesus as he wandered around the Mount of Transfiguration, having nowhere else to go.

The sorrowful journey of Jesus in the wilderness was due to the disbelief and failure of the ancestors to take responsibility. He searched for three years for someone who could understand the heart of heaven, but he could not fulfill that wish and had to ascend the mountain again. We must recall the sorrowful heart and footsteps of Jesus, who had to go up the mountain again. The footsteps Jesus took into the wilderness were steps taken with the standard of victory over Satan to embrace the nation, but the steps he took to the Mount of Transfiguration were steps taken to abandon all his resolutions and to prepare to give himself as a sacrifice to the nation, ready for death. At this time, if there is anyone who can recall the heart and appearance of Jesus as he ascended the mountain, and can empathize with that sorrow, then they will also be able to empathize with the sorrow of Jesus towards heaven, the sorrow of Jesus towards the nation, and the sorrow of Jesus towards the denomination.

The circumstances and solemn resolution of Jesus as he ascended the Mount of Transfiguration must be understood. When Jesus ascended the Mount of Transfiguration, three disciples followed him. They were in the position of chosen disciples representing the nation, but they could not establish any conditions of help for Jesus as he ascended the mountain.

When Jesus went out into the wilderness, angels came to minister to him, but when he ascended the Mount of Transfiguration, prepared to fight for the nation and ready to face death, even the three disciples who followed him could not minister to him. When we think of this, we cannot help but feel that Jesus' life, which began in sorrow and ended in sorrow, was filled with bitterness.
The Jesus knelt down and looked up to heaven, praying with all his heart and soul, saying that he would go according to the will of God as far as his strength would allow. He walked the path of public life for three years with a determination stronger than that of any historical ancestors, pouring out his loyalty, sincerity, and effort, yet he was driven away by his people and ostracized by his religious community. In a situation where not a single relative or disciple stood by him, Jesus lived a life of prayer towards heaven.

You must understand that Jesus' heart was filled with a sense of shame before God, feeling that after 4,000 years of God's labor with humanity, this was the outcome. Rather than feeling sorrow for his own lonely position, he felt a deep sense of embarrassment in presenting his feelings before God. In such a state of mind, Jesus could not harbor resentment towards his nation, his religious community, or even towards the fallen Adam and Eve. We must recognize that Jesus had no one to blame.

In the past, ancestors received comfort from heaven in times of sorrow, but Jesus realized that he could not even pray in his sorrow. I believe that before he prayed, tears of anguish must have first wet Jesus' knees. His appearance was that of the greatest sinner among sinners on earth. Before God, who had governed the history of labor for 4,000 years, Jesus found himself in a position where he could not present conditions for victory and had to appear alone on the Mount of Transfiguration, filled with sorrow, unable to open his mouth to pray.

Because of the dire circumstances, God sent Elijah and Moses to discuss Jesus' death in Jerusalem. Knowing that Jesus would be engulfed in sorrow, not only for his disciples but also for the people and future generations, he grieved over the past, present, and future. Feeling the need to save the Jewish people, who were facing a dead end with no hope, Jesus appeared before God with the same heart as Elijah, who cried out, "O my Father! Am I the only one left?" This heart of Jesus was truly one of deep sorrow.

We are well aware that our ancestors have left behind such a sorrowful history in their approach to heaven. God desired that the disciples on the Mount of Transfiguration would recognize their own sinful nature and share in Jesus' heart, or at least be concerned about the nation's sorrows on behalf of Jesus. He wanted them to comfort Jesus and pray for him, but the disciples had different thoughts. This has been the reality of the historical path our ancestors have walked until today.

Knowing that he was to die in Jerusalem, Jesus secretly prepared for that day. He felt the urgency of his impending death and the turmoil around him. He also knew that his beloved disciple would betray him, and he felt a serious need to conclude all matters of the world before going to the cross. This feeling lingered in his body and mind.

Understanding that he bore the mission of the Savior who must walk the final path before death, Jesus knew he had to set a direction for what lay ahead after passing through the path of death. He was concerned that his death would not eliminate the historical sorrows, the sorrows of the times, and the sorrows of the future, but that they would remain even after crossing the threshold of death. You must understand that this heart of Jesus was more solemn than ever.

No one on earth recognized Jesus, who was engulfed in such feelings. There was not a single disciple who understood his situation. Only God knew the plight of Jesus. Thus, Jesus bore a sorrowful heart that only he understood, filled with historical, temporal, and future grievances, and found himself in an environment where dark clouds and tragic barriers blocked his path, facing the misery of impending death. If this heart of Jesus was sorrowful, it was undoubtedly the most sorrowful heart on earth, and if it was filled with resentment and injustice, it was beyond comparison.

"My Father, if it is possible..." Who then did Jesus come to this earth for? He came on behalf of history, on behalf of the times, and for the nation and religious community, yet the path he walked was filled with sorrow. Jesus knew that his sorrow would not end with his own suffering, but that it would connect to historical sorrow, temporal sorrow, and future sorrow, which is why he was overwhelmed with anxiety.

For this reason, the place Jesus went to was the Garden of Gethsemane. We must become people who can mourn over this. The place where Jesus, the Savior of all mankind and King of all kings, expressed his final sorrow was not the house of a disciple, nor the Jewish religious community, nor the palace of the Jewish nation. It was the Garden of Gethsemane, a place where no one went in the deep night to discuss everything with God. We must recognize this fact.

Therefore, today, as saints in the last days, we must shed tears of sorrow to replace the tears that Jesus shed in the Garden of Gethsemane. We must also have the heart to portray the second appearance of Jesus. Only then can we connect with Jesus, who wept with historical sorrow for the times and the future, and who shed tears of blood and sweat three times in a miserable and pitiful situation.

"Father, if it is possible, let this cup pass from me." (Matthew 26:39) As Jesus prayed, if he was filled with resentment, it would have been beyond words, and if he was sorrowful, it would have been beyond measure. Because of Jesus, 4,000 years of history would pass in a single day, countless Israelites would perish overnight, the foundation of 4,000 years of providence would collapse in an hour, and the established Jewish community would disintegrate in an hour. When we think of this, the blood and sweat he shed were the blood and sweat that connected the distances of history, and the tears he shed were tears that connected the distances of history. However, we must recognize that the Jewish people at that time could not even dream of such a reality.

The disciples who followed Jesus swore to follow him wherever he went. But who inherited the bitter heart of Jesus, and who connected with the sorrowful tears of his heart? There was no one on earth who could do so. These matters were solely carried out by Jesus alone; there was no one among humanity who could inherit such feelings.

Thus, before facing death, Jesus prayed three times in the Garden of Gethsemane, "Abba, Father, all things are possible for you; take this cup away from me. Nevertheless, not what I will, but what you will." (Mark 14:36) This plea was a heartfelt cry that shook heaven and earth, a solemn declaration to prevent the powers of death from taking hold.

Therefore, the prayer in the Garden of Gethsemane must not become a dead prayer for Christian believers. Regardless of the era or century, the poignant and blood-soaked voice of this final plea must continually live in the hearts of humanity. Oh! As Jesus cried out to heaven, may there come a day when your heart resonates with his.

When we think of this, today’s saints in the last days must inherit the historical and solemn heart of Jesus, who cried out on Mount Calvary and in the Garden of Gethsemane. We must awaken Christians who are in the same position as the three disciples who slept in the Garden of Gethsemane. You must recognize that such a time is approaching.

And you must pray with the same heart that Jesus had when he ascended to the Garden of Gethsemane, saying, "My Father, if it is possible, let this cup pass from me." (Matthew 26:39), and become a group that prays, "Abba, Father! If possible, do not hand over our Messiah to the cross."

The Mountain that became the foundation of Jesus' blood and tears
When Jesus prayed three times, "My Father, if it is possible, let this cup pass from me." (Matthew 26:39), there was no one who prayed with the same heart, saying, "Abba, Father, if possible, let me be crucified instead of Jesus." You must understand that there was not a single chosen believer who could pray this way, nor a chosen nation.

The life path that Jesus walked was a continuous series of solemn events that took place on mountaintops, with no joy in any of it. Whenever he felt lonely, he sought the valley of the Mount of Olives, and whenever he felt sad, he spent time in the quiet forest, preaching silently. We must understand that he did not have the freedom to hold onto anyone and appeal to them about the deep contents of his heart.

Every time Jesus went up to the mountaintop to face the Father, he did so with sorrow and grief. Yet, amidst this, Jesus had a wish. What could that wish be? He recalled that all visible mountains and rivers were connected to God's tears and intertwined with the painful hearts of the ancestors, and he hoped that all these mountains and rivers would not become places of sorrow and tears, but rather become altars of joy and glory, offering songs of victory. This was indeed Jesus' wish. 

So, what should we feel when we look at the mountains today? If we recognize that our ancestors made solemn resolutions in the past to conclude all sorrowful histories on these mountains, we should also feel that these mountains hoped for our ancestors to triumph over the world of Satan. The mountains are places where Jesus prayed to establish the standards of victory in solemn scenes. Jesus must have waited for the day when he could build an altar of victory and glory on these mountains and say, "Abba, Father, let me enjoy glory because of me." Therefore, when you look at the mountains, you must feel that they are the mountains that became the foundation of Jesus' blood and tears.

Perhaps Jesus held onto a blade of grass in the Garden of Gethsemane and cried out, or he might have clung to a rock and made his plea. Thus, that rock and that grass could share in the heart of Jesus, who prayed throughout the night, while the people of that time could not. We must recognize this fact.

Furthermore, we must lament the sorrowful state of humanity, feeling ashamed to look at all creation and the mountains, realizing that we should not become like the Jewish people who drove Jesus away from the mountains when the Lord returns to this earth in the last days. We must welcome the Lord into our homes, into society, and into the nation. We must welcome the Lord wherever we are, even on the mountaintops. Thus, you must be able to present the Lord before heaven as a being of joy and glory. You must also recognize that you have the responsibility to prepare an environment where the Lord's words will not be words of sorrow, but words filled with joy and love.

Mountains! Mountains! The mountains that received the tears of God, who lamented the history of sorrow, do not look upon any existence on this earth, or towards creation, or the historical path, or this era with sorrowful tears. God is facing every existence on this earth with a heart filled with sorrow.

Beloved! You must understand the path of Jesus, who walked only towards the mountains, starting from the mountains. Jesus prepared the conditions for victory on the mountaintop and also in his living environment. You must recognize that Jesus was one who hoped to meet God even on the mountaintop.

This was the historical heart of Jesus, who went to the mountains to establish a standard of victory, his temporal steps, and also his hope. We must understand this.

Furthermore, we must fight against Satan in today's wilderness on behalf of Jesus, and we must be prepared to fight for the nation and the world, just as Jesus fought on the Mount of Transfiguration, ready to face death. We must be able to cry out to our Heavenly Father with the heart of Jesus, who formed historical connections in the Garden of Gethsemane before facing death. We must be able to inherit the heart of heaven that desires to connect with this earth with a heart that is bursting with emotion.

And if you do not establish a being through whom the heart of heaven can be connected, remember that the labor of Jesus on the mountaintop will be in vain.

<Prayer> Father! We know that humanity, seeking religion, needs great mountains. We are well aware that all the great figures in history have formed connections with mountains, expressing their situations and determining the standards of life and death, victory and defeat alongside the mountains.

Jesus, as the representative of humanity, walked to the mountaintop, and the place where he connected his heart to appeal to heaven was the mountaintop.

We recognize that it was the mountains that established such historical connections, so please allow your sons and daughters to appear on the mountaintops scattered across this beautiful land of Korea. Let us become proud beings who can repay the historical grievances that were formed on the mountains by giving glory to God.

To become such beings, we must understand that not only as individuals but also as families, societies, religions, nations, and the world, we must pass through these mountaintops. Today, may we be guided to emulate the heart of Jesus, who ascended and descended the mountains on behalf of heaven and earth, and may we follow in his footsteps. Until the day we can build an altar of victory on the mountaintop and sing praises of Hosanna, may we be tireless sons and daughters who fight without knowing fatigue or retreat.

Father! We know that with such determination and resolution, you will cooperate with us, so please lead us to break through any obstacles with that determined mind, and if it is your will, let us become true sons and daughters who bear the responsibility to connect with your heart. the history of humanity. God has been striving to hold onto fallen humanity and carry out the providence of salvation. When we humans were lost in sin, there was someone who sought us out, cared for us, and introduced us to welfare. This person is not our beloved parents, nor any child or spouse we are emotionally connected to. They are not a nation, nor any sage or philosopher; they are God, a fact that you must keep in mind.

God has worked tirelessly to pave the way for the entirety of human hope up to this day. Furthermore, to resolve our circumstances and feelings, and to untangle all our troubles, He has been laboring and fighting without rest. You must not forget that God has been carrying out the mission of a pioneer throughout history until now.

Heaven has been providentially working without change, even though humanity has remained ignorant of the task of pioneering for 4,000 long years from the fall of Adam until the coming of Jesus. God has been moving toward the goal of a garden of happiness with a single day's hope for humanity. We are well aware that humanity has taken steps through history toward that world.

After the fall of humanity, God has worked through individuals and nations for 4,000 years, establishing the nation of Israel to fulfill His will.
4,000 years of labor have been handed over to Jesus as a master who can transfer the overall mission of heaven and the heart and wishes of heaven. However, we know well that the Jewish people who believed at that time and the Israelites who prided themselves on being the chosen people did not know who He was. Thus, the Israelite nation, chosen by God through His labor, could not receive Jesus Christ, whom He sent to fulfill His labor, and neither could the denominations, nor anyone in society or family. As a result, the pioneering intention that God wished for was frustrated, and the Israelite nation, which should have walked the path of fulfillment through Jesus, went the path of failure, that is, the path of death. God worked hard on the path of pioneering, and Jesus came with the glorious mission to repay heaven's labor by fulfilling this pioneering purpose. However, since the chosen people did not recognize Jesus and expelled Him, we must understand that Jesus had to stand again in the position of a pioneer on behalf of the Israelite nation that had been established through 4,000 years of labor before heaven. Jesus came with the responsibility to build the world of ideals that the chosen nation hoped for. Yet, the Israelite nation, which was hoping for the Messiah, did not realize that the Jesus who appeared was the Messiah they longed for. Here, the scene of heaven's sorrow and tragedy unfolded in a new direction. In light of this fact, we must have a heart that can grieve on behalf of God and a heart that can grieve on behalf of Jesus. If we do not have such a heart, we cannot understand God's heart, which has come to pioneer for humanity, nor can we understand the heart of Jesus, who appeared with the intention of a pioneer before the chosen nation. To establish the foundation of happiness and the garden of hope, the denominations and the nation had to go together with Jesus leading the way through the valley of death, and they also had to go together when Jesus went through the hill of happiness and joy. Heaven established an unbreakable heavenly connection over 4,000 years, but our ancestors betrayed the connection with heaven and betrayed the merits of heaven's pioneering work, and we must feel deep sorrow over these facts.

**Jesus' Preparation Period**  
About 2,000 years ago, Jesus looked upon the Israelite nation, which harbored elements of disbelief, with a sorrowful heart. He also saw that the Jewish denomination, which should have been established on the foundation of heavenly heart, was caught up in the formal aspects of the law received by Moses and had departed from the position of the heavenly altar. Looking at the Israelite nation, which did not know where they should live or what direction they should go, Jesus realized that God had sent Him with the purpose of establishing Himself through the 4,000 years of pioneering work and raising these people to become a group that would pioneer a new world. At that moment, we must understand that Jesus' heart could not help but be filled with a heavy resolve. After being born in a stable, He lived a lonely life, helping His father Joseph, who was a carpenter. His life was limited by his circumstances, but his ideals were to reach beyond the Israelite nation and the world to the entire universe, and He lived in such a manner. However, when He thought that even Joseph, who commanded Him, and His brothers who followed Him did not know this fact, Jesus could not help but be in a position of indescribable sorrow. When Jesus came to understand the realities of the world, the internal heart that permeated God's providence, and the circumstances of the earth in which He was placed, He hoped that these feelings, circumstances, and realities would unite and move toward the direction God desired. Nevertheless, God's heart moved according to His heart, Jesus' circumstances moved according to His circumstances, and the realities of the world moved chaotically according to their own ways. What kind of resolution and determination did Jesus have when He looked at this fact? After going through 30 years of preparation, He resolved to fulfill God's will through a practical path. While looking forward to that moment, the more sorrowful His heart became, the more He cried out to heaven, and the more hopeless the path before Him seemed, the more He sought to resolve that situation through humanity. The closer God's heart came to Him, the closer the world should have come to Him, and the chosen nation and the denomination established by heaven should have come close to Him, but contrary to God, the nation felt increasingly distant, and the life of Jesus was undoubtedly a serious life that you cannot imagine. 

During this time, Jesus did not blame the people who did not understand the serious circumstances of heaven, but thought that He had to penetrate their lives, open their hearts, and eventually embrace their hearts. This was Jesus. Therefore, you must consider that there was a sorrowful situation in which He could not claim, "I am the Savior you desire." Jesus had to make a new resolution in the face of such adversity. Knowing that the foundation established by heaven over 4,000 years was crumbling, Jesus held a heavy heart to fight again for the Israelite nation. This is something we do not know today. Thus, in such an environment, Jesus prayed inwardly to heaven, saying, "O God, grant me strength. O God, grant me a new direction. O God, allow me to have a heavy resolve both inwardly and outwardly." We must again reflect on the fact that He lived in silence, questioning and answering Himself for 30 long years. 

In this position, what kind of sense of mission did Jesus have in carrying out the mission of a pioneer on behalf of God, who is intangible? He felt the mission to open the closed gates of heaven and build the kingdom of heaven for heaven, and for the earth, He felt the mission to pioneer the tangled and closed hearts of all people, the world of hearts that were closed to heaven. Furthermore, Jesus felt that there was a mission to pioneer this sinful world in which humanity lives once again. Jesus resolved that He could not interrupt the restoration providence that God had worked hard on for 4,000 years, and even if the Israelite nation betrayed God, He must walk without changing and fulfill that one purpose. In other words, when Jesus thought of the internal connection that heaven moved through, He could not help but establish such a heavy resolve within Himself. For Jesus, whether He could become a pioneer who could fulfill this mission in the environment of that time was an important issue. When He became such a pioneer, Jesus could appear on behalf of the nation, on behalf of the chosen people, and on behalf of history before God, and God could trust His resolve and He could appear as a figure that God could boast about. 

**Jesus' Efforts to Fulfill His Mission**  
So how did Jesus fulfill this mission? He went through a preparation period. Thus, Jesus sought to graft the hearts of humanity onto the heart of heaven, and He sought to achieve an integrated ideology where heaven and earth could move together, where heaven and humanity could be one, where earth and heaven could be one, and where heaven and humanity could be one. We must understand that Jesus' resolve to become a pioneer who would achieve such a position was incredibly serious. He established Himself for the chosen Israel and also for all created beings on earth; even if the earth betrayed Him, He could not abandon Himself because the nation remained, and even if the nation betrayed Him, He could not abandon Himself because heaven remained. Therefore, He could not help but appear with a heavy resolve and determination from His inner heart. For this reason, we must understand that the more He felt the heart of resentment to reclaim the world from Satan, the more His heart exploded with hatred toward the enemy, and the more it exploded, the more He felt infinite sorrow. 

During this period filled with such a heart, Jesus must have sworn in his heart hundreds, thousands, and tens of thousands of times. When reflecting on the history of the Israelite chosen people who had come on behalf of heaven for 4,000 years, He realized that the Israelite nation had not been on heaven's side. When He became aware of this, Jesus anticipated that there would be difficult persecutions in moving toward this path and made a new resolution. God earnestly desires to find humanity living in such a miserable environment even today. Jesus felt the responsibility to resolve the inability of heaven and humanity, who were struggling to connect. Therefore, when He saw that the Israelite nation could not go in the direction established by heaven, He felt an infinitely sorrowful heart. Moreover, when He thought about the earth that could not become a stepping stone for God to come and could not become a foundation for good, the earth that Satan was ruling and ravaging, He could not help but feel indescribable sorrow, thinking about the 4,000 years of labor. 

Every time Jesus sank into such sorrow, He resolved that He would fight on heaven's side for humanity and this earth, and no matter what persecution or difficulty came, He would overcome it. Thus, the commitment He made during the 30 years of preparation was a resolution to engage in a great battle in the practical path ahead. Even if He became a sacrifice of rejection before the Israelite nation in a position of disbelief, He resolved that He must go this way and find ways to establish it. He thought of plans that no one else could conceive of, saying that if they believed, they would do this, and if they did not believe, they would do that, and He prayed to heaven in a way that no one else could worry about. Furthermore, while growing up in the household of Joseph the carpenter for 30 years, even when His brothers rejoiced, He could not show a joyful face, and even when relatives and all gatherings in the church were happy, He could not express joy. You must understand that this was because the direction heaven desired and the direction humanity thought were so different. When He looked at this, the greater the difference, the firmer His resolve became, and the greater the difference, the more He thought that it was something He would have to fill in the future. 

However, even though He had many things to say, Jesus had to keep His mouth shut. Even though He had a deep desire to preach while traveling around the regions of Israel, He could not help but assist His family during the sorrowful 30 years of preparation. 

**Resolution as a Pioneer**  
What was Jesus' resolution as a pioneer during the 30 years of preparation? It was the determination that even if there was a hill of death, He would go. Even if there was a path of persecution, He would go. Even if there were things that would lead to ruin, He would go. Thus, during this preparation period, Jesus made a lifelong commitment that he could clear away his living environment, clear away the ideals of life for himself, clear away all national connections, and even clear away the forms of the Jewish denomination that emphasized the Old Testament and laws. Jesus, who had to pioneer the kingdom of heaven and the hearts of all humanity, lived every day in a manner where his heart would visit the realm of God's ideals several times a day. You must understand that this was Jesus. 

Although the people of the earth did not recognize the inner sorrow of the 30 years of preparation, only God stood by Jesus' side. Whether Jesus was in a place where He was pushing wood with a plane, in a place where He was carving wood with a chisel, or in a place where He was cutting wood with a saw, even when He stayed in a place to eat and rest, His heart wished to feel God's heart and circumstances, and He wished for the kingdom of heaven, which was God's wish, to be established, and He never forgot that at any moment. 

Moreover, even if He had to abandon the 4,000 years of history, He could not abandon such values, and even if He abandoned the chosen Israel, He could not abandon such values, and even if He abandoned the chosen denomination, He could not abandon this. He felt deeply in His heart and in His bones and flesh that He could abandon everything, but not this. Thus, the life of Jesus, who was preparing while looking forward to a day of hope with a heart that could move thoroughly, was a continuous life of seriousness that you must understand. 

You should once again picture the heart of Jesus, who was preparing for a day and a time. Even though what He wore was shabby and His appearance looked sorrowful, His gaze was not inferior to any conqueror or pioneer of the earth. His gaze was connected to the heart of heaven, and He had an astonishing gaze that could pierce through the universe. Therefore, we cannot help but think that He could not help but become a figure of a suffering and pitiful person, and He could not help but have a sorrowful appearance. 

When we reflect on these facts, we can see that as Jesus' heart grew stronger in holding onto the heart of God, who had worked hard through the historical path, His concern grew that the Israelite nation might become a nation of disbelief, and He was infinitely worried that they might become apostles of disbelief or disciples of disbelief. Jesus spent the 30 years of preparation with such a heart in silence. 

Even if the fervent heart of Jesus standing on heaven's side grew stronger, it was not for His own sake. Even if His gaze, burning with heaven's hope, was serious while looking at the world, it was not for His own desires. We must understand that His gaze was solely for the Israelite nation, and His heart was also for the Israelite nation and for the whole world. That is why Jesus shed infinite tears of sorrow. During that preparation period, Jesus did not only resolve to face the hill of the cross once. Whenever there was a rumor of someone dying, He felt that He was the one who had to revive that person hundreds of times. Whenever someone was unjustly persecuted and was in a pitiful situation, He changed that situation into His own. You must understand the heart of Jesus, who looked at the horrific realities of society at that time as empirical offerings occurring on the practical path of His own life. 

**Jesus' Public Life Filled with Trials and Suffering**  
Jesus, who came 2,000 years ago, lived through a 30-year preparation period filled with sorrow.
Before Jesus, there was not a single person who could understand Him, worship Him, or serve Him with a sincere heart. There was not even a single ugly crippled person. This is truly a sad fact. If there had been such a person, we, the descendants of today, could at least hold our heads high. When we think about this, we must recognize that we are infinitely indebted to Heaven.

Jesus had boundless expectations as he looked at the 30 years of preparation by John the Baptist. Thus, Jesus, who was hoping for a day to start His public ministry, finally stepped into the practical process after the preparation period. At that time, He thought the nation would welcome Him, or perhaps John the Baptist would welcome Him, but both the nation and John the Baptist were cold and opposed Him. The Jewish sect also opposed Him. Jesus, who had come out with a solemn resolution during the preparation period, found Himself in a tragic situation where He had to fight against the nation of Israel instead of the world. You must understand this. Therefore, we must recognize that the nation of Israel, which had worked hard for 4,000 years to prepare for the Messiah, had to take on the mission of pioneering from the very bottom once again.

Here, we must consider that the entire foundation that God had built over 4,000 years collapsed, and we must think about the sorrow of Jesus, who could not appear before the entire people with the absoluteness of the historical path that God had governed immediately after the fall of Adam and Eve. He had come to the chosen people, but was instead chased away by them. So where did Jesus go? The nation of Israel, which Heaven had labored for 4,000 years, betrayed Heaven and stood in the position of Satan. Who could understand the sorrowful heart of Jesus as He looked upon this?

Thus, Jesus went into the wilderness and fasted for 40 days. You may not have realized that the Jesus you believe in today was such a pitiful figure. The only begotten Son of Heaven, the Prince of Heaven, came to the human world, was rejected by humans, went into the wilderness without food, and was tested before Satan, who was an enemy of God. The people of that time did not know this fact. How could we express God's anger as He looked upon the sorrowful path of Jesus?

Feeling the pain in His heart due to anger, Jesus knew that Heaven would be concerned about His own sorrow. Therefore, He did not express His own sorrow and had profound filial piety towards Heaven. When we recall such a Jesus, we must understand that He felt the heart of God, who was worried for Him, leaving the state where Adam betrayed Heaven in the Garden of Eden. Thus, even though He was in a position to pray for His own sorrow, He avoided this and suppressed His angry heart to comfort Heaven, opening a hopeful path to return to God through the sorrow of the fall. Jesus resolved to establish this as a practical path during the 30 years of preparation. He knew that His steps would have to make the nation an enemy.

When we think about this, we can see that our ancestors created a history of sorrow due to their mistakes. Heaven hoped that the disciples on the Mount of Transfiguration would comfort Jesus with the same heart, worrying about the national sorrow, and pray on His behalf. These were the disciples who were to build such an altar. However, the disciples were only thinking about other things. Thus, Jesus, who was in a position to announce a day of death through Jerusalem, made a new resolution and lived a life preparing for that day.

The reality of Jesus as a pioneer
The effort of Jesus to establish disciples
So what is God's strategy? To find one person, Heaven must first bear the value of that person. This is the providence of Heaven. To find a family, Heaven must bear the burden equivalent to that family before taking it. Therefore, to re-establish a nation, God must first receive a blow of that magnitude. Jesus understood that this was Heaven's strategy in the practical path.

As Jesus, who was to represent God, sought to find the nation, He became a sacrifice for individuals, families, denominations, and nations, walking the sacrificial path of pioneering that was beaten. You must understand this. Jesus, who appeared with this ideological method of practice, sought to find His companions from the prepared Jewish sect, but there was not a single person to welcome Him. Even today, in the context of Korea, we know that fishermen are not treated as people and are extremely poor. We must understand what position Jesus was in when He approached the ignorant fishermen 2,000 years ago. Did Peter and others, as seen in the Bible, immediately follow Jesus after being moved by His words? Absolutely not. The Bible does not reveal the practical content behind this.

Jesus, who was forsaken by the nation, appeared as a laborer, became a friend of fishermen, shared their circumstances, became a friend who shared their hearts, and became a friend who shared their wishes, fighting with the heart to fulfill whatever they desired, even at the cost of His life. Because He had this emotional content and ideological foundation, fishermen like Peter were able to follow Him.

So what did Jesus do with the ignorant disciples for three years? Just as God had worked and served for 4,000 years to establish the nation of Israel, Jesus established them and lived a life of service. Jesus, who chose the twelve disciples, had great hopes for them. He was sent by Heaven to move the Jewish sect and govern the priests and all the scribes. Therefore, His ideals were great, His desires were great, and His emotional standards were high. You must understand that the priests and scribes of that time, who failed to recognize Jesus, who appeared as a pioneer with God's substantial ideals, were more pitiful than Adam and Eve right after the fall.

Seeing this crowd, what did Jesus do? Heaven had gone through a path of service for 4,000 years to establish the chosen people, and Jesus walked through that historical tradition in His three years of public ministry. Therefore, even if Jesus had something He wanted to eat, or even if food was available, He forgot it and sought the disciples. If there was clothing, He did not think of His own nakedness but gave it to the disciples. If there was a comfortable place, He would place the disciples there while He remained in a humble position. You must understand that Jesus lived His three years of public ministry with such a heart and such an ideal, and it had to achieve victorious results, yet He did not obtain such results.

Disciples who did not follow Jesus' teachings
The disciples, who did not understand Jesus' heart, played games to rise to high positions using Him. Knowing this, Jesus wept and struck the ground, feeling that there was no way to relieve His heart, and even when He cried out to Heaven, He had no way to ease His sorrow. However, because there was a path of mission that He could not avoid, He suppressed His heart and said to the disciples, "Whoever exalts himself will be humbled, and whoever humbles himself will be exalted" (Matthew 23:12). You must understand that He was reaffirming the determination that was deeply embedded in His heart.

At that time, the disciples who heard this thought it was Jesus' words and had nothing to do with them. Think about how Jesus felt when the mother of John asked to place her two sons at His right and left in glory. Jesus was a pitiful figure. Despite Jesus teaching and admonishing the disciples in such a way, they did not understand His intention.

Therefore, as the following crowd grew larger, the disciples showed actions that indicated their joy, but they could not stand in a sacrificial position that honored and served Jesus, following the example He had shown them through His actions. Rather, because of the disciples, it became difficult for others to come before Jesus. Nevertheless, Jesus knew that the disciples had a responsibility to fulfill the cries of the denomination, and that the denomination had a responsibility to fulfill the cries of the nation, and that the nation had a responsibility to fulfill the cries of the world, and that the world had a responsibility to fulfill the cries of Heaven.

However, no one understood this heart of His. For Jesus, who was in such a situation, there could not have been greater sorrow than the sorrow He felt when He looked upon the few disciples who only asked for Himself. Thus, Jesus, with all His efforts, fed the saints when they were hungry, comforted them when they cried, and introduced the blessings of Heaven through the Beatitudes when they were discouraged. We must understand that the words of the Gospel express the painful heart of Jesus, who worried that they might be discouraged or fall away as He led them.

Furthermore, even though the disciples should have drawn closer to Him upon hearing His words, they moved further away. You must feel the heart of Jesus as He looked upon this. Even when He wrapped a towel around His head and took a basin to wash the disciples' feet, He asserted that His duty was to serve. He knew that only by doing this could He establish a connection with Heaven, and thus He could not avoid it. You must understand that Jesus felt sorrow while looking at the disciples.

The miracles performed by Jesus on the path of restoration were not done out of joy. If you think that He performed miracles because He was happy and comfortable, that is a great misunderstanding. There was a situation where He had no place to lay His body on this earth and no one to rely on in this universe, so He had no choice but to appeal to Heaven. You must look upon the earnest appearance of Jesus, who was in such a solemn state.

When He was in a sorrowful situation where He could not show compassion to them, He raised His hands and called out, "Father!" It was from this moment that miracles occurred. We must understand that the miracles were manifestations of His sorrowful cries in a scene so sad that His bones and flesh felt like they were melting away. Do not think that Jesus performed these miracles out of negligence or pleasure.

In the fields of Bethsaida, a crowd of over 5,000 cried out, "Jesus, You are our Savior and the leader of the chosen people of Israel!" They came when it was beneficial for them, but as time passed and Jesus' spiritual standards, circumstances, and criteria changed, they betrayed Him and turned away. This was the phenomenon that occurred in the practical path Jesus walked.

The heart of Jesus on the practical path
However, no matter how external conditions changed, Jesus' heart could not change, nor could His path. This path was the path of destiny that fallen humanity must inevitably take, yet the nation of Israel, which should have followed it, betrayed Jesus, and the following crowd betrayed Him, and even the disciples, who should have believed in and served Him, differed in heart, circumstances, and hopes. You must understand that there were many scenes that evoked sorrow in Jesus' gaze as He looked upon this.

However, Jesus knew that He personally had to suffer persecution, that He had to suffer persecution on a familial level, and that He had to suffer persecution on a denominational, national, and global level before the Roman Empire. He quietly continued on His way. As He crossed the Mount of Transfiguration to find Calvary, He was prepared to face any persecution or suffering that might come. He had the resolve that He must overcome what He had to overcome for His time. If He could not overcome it, the preparation path would manifest as a sorrowful aspect, so He moved toward the hill of death, the hill of suffering. To fulfill this purpose, He resolved to share His blood and flesh as a sacrificial offering for humanity. This was the heart of Jesus, who walked with a determination filled with Heaven's heart. Yet, no one knew that He was walking to fulfill the determination He had made during the preparation period. You must understand this.

Jesus, who could not blame the many crowds that rejected Him, was more sensitive and had a greater sense of indignation than anyone else. He also felt a sense of responsibility that He had to pioneer the path of purpose centered on the nation of Israel. Knowing the heart of God that had been poured out through 4,000 years of connection, Jesus could not abandon the nation. Even if they rejected Him, He prayed, "Please save them through me," and even when the disciples betrayed Him, He prayed, "Please fulfill the will of salvation through me." Jesus walked this path.

The twelve disciples, who vowed to die with Him or live with Him, said, "Lord! Wherever You go, we will go with You." This was said when Jesus was about to reveal the Gospel. The resolve of the following disciples to say, "I will follow wherever You go," was similar to the heart of Jesus when He first started and when He was heading toward Gethsemane.

He said, "Foxes have holes, and birds of the air have nests, but the Son of Man has nowhere to lay His head," and entrusted His body, head, and heart to the embrace of the Father. This prayer was to hold on to God, who had labored through the sighs and adversities of entangled humanity, and to entrust His own sorrowful heart. This was the decisive prayer in the Garden of Gethsemane. With this promise established, the steps He took to fulfill it were the image of Jesus walking the path of Golgotha with the cross on His back. Jesus resolved to be offered as a sacrifice in place of the path that God had labored for 4,000 years. This was the determination of Jesus, who walked forward to offer Himself as a sacrificial offering before humanity, which had betrayed and failed to understand God's heart regarding the providence of that time. Thus, the practical path of Jesus also ended in sorrow.
Thus, he completed his journey of practice without even having the companionship of a single person. This was true in his external feelings and in his practical living environment as well. For this reason, Jesus, as a sacrificial offering of history, shed his blood alone, prepared to face death in order to present a new path of life to humanity, and you must understand that this was his journey of practice.

The providential history that returned after being struck
Before Jesus died on the cross, while shedding blood, he prayed, "My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?" (Matthew 27:46) and at the end of this prayer, he said, "It is finished." (John 19:30) Here, the statement "It is finished" does not mean that he completed the ideological world that must be achieved centered on the nation, but rather that he fulfilled the resolution he had made to act in a way that would lead to the path of sorrow during the 30 years of preparation. We must understand that this statement is not a joyful one, but rather a declaration of Jesus's sorrowful heart to all humanity. We must recognize that it was his final testament to express that sorrow to those who do not understand.

For this reason, humanity hopes for the day when we can truly say that we have completed the internal sorrowful path of Jesus. That day is the day of the Second Coming, and you must understand this. You need to know this. The path that Jesus determined to take in confronting the world of Satan was precisely the path of the cross, and today, Christians around the world are also following that path. Look, heaven has said it will come and find you. Since the nation betrayed him and even the twelve apostles denied Jesus, the one who was resurrected and sought was none other than the twelve disciples. Heaven comes and finds in this way. Furthermore, Stephen, who believed in Jesus, was stoned to death. When Stephen, who was on heaven's side, was killed, heaven sought Saul instead. Just as Jesus resurrected and sought out the disciples who had betrayed him, at a time when Jesus's disciples were being killed, he exercised the authority of resurrection and took Saul, which means he came and found him. After Saul changed his name to Paul, he was welcomed instead of the twelve disciples. Who would have thought that Paul, who was being chased and persecuted, would become the apostle among apostles and lay the foundation of Christianity!

So, who struck Jesus? The Roman soldiers struck him, and the entire nation of Israel struck him. Among them, who was the primary instigator? It was Rome. For this reason, the disciples of Jesus had the principle left to atone for what Jesus suffered, so they entered Rome and received punishment in his place. The twelve apostles, the seventy disciples, and the countless crowds who believed had a principle left to atone for what they suffered on behalf of the nation, so Rome could not simply pass by after striking.

After the Roman Empire era and through the feudal society where the Catholic Church flourished, during the Reformation period, the corrupt Catholic Church was struck when Luther rebelled. In this way, the Protestant Church, which had been struck, later left that place and centered on the heavenly way, crossing the Atlantic, boasting of their achievements, and establishing the culture that built today's America. This indicates that it was established through the persecuted Christian groups following the worldly external Canaan.

Now, as Israel has developed into a representative democratic nation, it is time for heaven to once again seek out a group that will be struck. Therefore, this is a historical turning point. History is seeking out a group that will be struck. Thus, at this time, a group that is being persecuted and chased should emerge among the denominations and in democratic nations. The group that is being persecuted has a different will and ideology from the existing ones. Why? Because the ideology that Jesus brought is not an earthly ideology but a heavenly ideology, fundamentally different from the ideologies that were accepted on earth. The people who wish to live according to this new ideology must go through a transformative process of cosmic renewal, as we know through history.

So, what kind of group should appear at that moment? In the end times of history, a blessed group of believers who follow the path of Jesus on Golgotha must emerge, even if they are being pushed and chased toward the summit of Golgotha. Therefore, we must not forget that it is time for a denomination that carries the burden of Golgotha, not just personally but in a Christian or denominational sense, to emerge.

What Jesus was meant to possess, he was struck and possessed. He was struck by Rome, thus he possessed Rome. Because of this, he carried out the movement for the restoration of denominations, nations, and the world, and personally walked the path of Golgotha. Therefore, today, a denomination that is being struck, that is, a denomination walking the path of Golgotha, must emerge, and a nation that is also walking the path of Golgotha must emerge. In the end, this is the official path to heaven.

We must prepare to meet the day when we can say we have completed it without dying before heaven.

Only then can you replace what Jesus could not accomplish on this earth as a pioneer of both sides. Just as Jesus could not strike those who pursued him and instead prayed for the nation and the enemies, today we must have the generosity to hold onto such a group and bless them, and we must have the determination to hold onto heaven beyond death. Only then can we become global sons and daughters who can embrace the love of God on the day of glory and become pioneers of a new world. Please keep this in mind.
